<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">VA - Burial Benefits - Presidential Memorial Certificates</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>A Presidential Memorial Certificate (PMC) is an engraved paper certificate, signed by the current... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="VA - Burial Benefits - Presidential Memorial Certificates" data-agency="U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>A <a href="https://www.cem.va.gov/cem/pmc.asp" target="_blank">Presidential Memorial Certificate</a> (PMC) is an engraved paper certificate, signed by the current President, to honor the memory of honorably discharged Veterans.</p>

<p>To learn more, visit the <a href="https://www.cem.va.gov/" target="_blank">National Cemetery Administration</a> website.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>Eligible recipients, including the Veteran's next of kin and loved ones, or someone acting on their behalf, may apply for a PMC. You may request more than one certificate.</p>

<p>You may not request a PMC for a living Veteran.</p>

<p>A Veteran must have an honorable discharge or a general discharge under honorable conditions. Certain National Guard and Reserve members may also qualify. Commissioned Officers of the Public Health Service (PHS) and National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) qualify as active duty members and Veterans once discharged.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>To make a request, eligible recipients, or someone acting on their behalf, must complete the <a href="https://www.va.gov/vaforms/va/pdf/VA40-0247.pdf" target="_blank">Presidential Memorial Certificate Request Form</a> (VA Form 40-0247, PDF, 721 KB). You can submit the form using one of the methods below:</p>

<ul>
	<li>In person at any VA regional office. You can use our <a href="https://www.va.gov/directory/guide/home.asp" target="_blank">Find Locations</a> page to find your state office.</li>
	<li>By fax at 1-800-445-7143. For instructions, read <a href="https://www.cem.va.gov/cem/faxpmc.asp" target="_blank">Order a PMC Using Our Toll Free Fax.</a></li>
	<li>By mail:</li>
</ul>

<p style="margin-left: 35.1pt;">Presidential Memorial Certificates (41B3)<br />
National Cemetery Administration<br />
5109 Russell Road<br />
Quantico, VA 22134-3903</p>

<p>We do not accept requests via email.</p>

<p>You must include a copy of both the Veterans discharge and death certificates. We cant process a request without proof of honorable military service. Please send copies only. We will not return original documents.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions about a PMC you received, a request youve already sent, or the program in general, please<a href="https://www.va.gov/landing2_contact.htm" target="_blank">Contact Us</a>.</p>

<p>To apply for other Veterans benefits and view your status, open a free eBenefits Premium account. eBenefits is a one-stop resource for Department of Defense (DoD) and VA benefits and services. Veterans, Servicemembers, and their families may open eBenefits accounts.</p>

<p>With a Premium account you can handle self-service actions like the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Check claim status.</li>
	<li>Handle GI Bill enrollment.</li>
	<li>Get copies of civil service preference letters, DD214, and other personal information.</li>
</ul>

<p>Visit <a href="https://www.ebenefits.va.gov/" target="_blank">eBenefits</a> to learn more or register for an account.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">VA - Burial Benefits - Partial Reimbursement of Expenses</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) burial allowance is a monetary benefit that can help to pay for an eligible Veteran's burial and funeral costs. VA may grant... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="VA - Burial Benefits - Partial Reimbursement of Expenses" data-agency="U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) burial allowance is a monetary benefit that can help to pay for an eligible Veteran's burial and funeral costs. VA may grant additional benefits for plot, interment, or transportation allowances.</p>

<p>To learn more, visit the <a href="https://benefits.va.gov/benefits/" target="_blank">Veterans Benefits Administration</a> website and read the <a href="https://www.benefits.va.gov/BENEFITS/factsheets/burials/Burial.pdf" target="_blank">Burial and Plot Interment Allowance</a> (PDF, 141 KB) fact sheet.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>VA automatically pays a burial benefit to the eligible surviving spouse of record upon report of a Veterans death. If no surviving spouse is of record, VA will pay the first living person from the list below to file a claim:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Veteran's surviving spouse, OR</li>
	<li>Survivor of a legal union with the Veteran, OR</li>
	<li>Veteran's children, regardless of age, OR</li>
	<li>Veteran's parents or surviving parent, OR</li>
	<li>Executor or administrator of the Veterans estate, OR</li>
	<li>A person acting for the Veterans estate.</li>
</ul>

<p>To qualify for benefits, a Veteran must have been discharged under conditions other than dishonorably and must meet at least one of the conditions below:</p>

<ul>
	<li>They died as a result of a service-related disability, OR</li>
	<li>They were receiving or entitled to receive VA pension or compensation at the time of death, OR</li>
	<li>They died while admitted in a VA medical facility or while receiving care under a VA contract at a non-VA facility, OR </li>
	<li>They died while a patient at a VA-approved state nursing home, OR</li>
	<li>They had a claim pending prior to their date of death and would have been entitled to VA compensation or pension from a date prior to the date of death, OR</li>
	<li>They died while traveling to or from a specified place for examination, treatment, or care, under proper authorization and at VA expense.</li>
</ul>

<p>These requirements do not apply for Veterans whose remains are unclaimed.</p>

<p>National Guard and Reserve members who serve in active-duty military service (other than for training) may qualify.</p>

<p>Commissioned Officers of the Public Health Service (PHS) and National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) may qualify as active duty members and Veterans once discharged.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>Visit the <a href="https://www.vets.gov/burials-and-memorials/application/530/introduction" target="_blank">Apply for burial benefits</a> page to learn more and apply online. You may also download and submit an <a href="https://www.vba.va.gov/pubs/forms/VBA-21P-530-ARE.pdf" target="_blank">Application for Burial Benefits</a> (VA Form 21P-530, PDF, 933 KB). Mail or fax your application to your states VA regional office. You can look up their address on our <a href="https://www.va.gov/directory/guide/home.asp" target="_blank">Find Locations</a> page.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions, call VA:</p>

<ul>
	<li>1-800-827-1000 or 1-877-294-6380</li>
	<li>TTY 1-800-829-4833</li>
</ul>

<p>To apply for other Veterans benefits and view your status, open a free eBenefits Premium account. eBenefits is a one-stop resource for Department of Defense (DoD) and VA benefits and services. Veterans, Servicemembers, and their families may open eBenefits accounts.</p>

<p>With a Premium account you can handle self-service actions like the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Check claim status.</li>
	<li>Handle GI Bill enrollment.</li>
	<li>Get copies of civil service preference letters, DD214, and other personal information.</li>
</ul>

<p>Visit <a href="https://www.ebenefits.va.gov/" target="_blank">eBenefits</a> to learn more or register for an account.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">VA - Burial Benefits - Headstones, Markers, and Medallions for Placement in Private Cemeteries</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) furnishes upon request, at no charge, a government headstone or marker for the unmarked grave of any deceased, eligible Veteran in... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="VA - Burial Benefits - Headstones, Markers, and Medallions for Placement in Private Cemeteries" data-agency="U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) furnishes upon request, at no charge, a government headstone or marker for the unmarked grave of any deceased, eligible Veteran in any cemetery around the world. Regardless of their date of death.</p>

<p>If the Veteran died on or after November 1, 1990, and their grave is marked with a private headstone or marker, they may also qualify for a headstone or marker to supplement the grave. Or you may get a medallion to fasten to the private headstone. Niche markers are also available to mark columbaria for cremated remains.</p>

<p>You may visit the National Cemetery Administration <a href="http://www.cem.va.gov/hm_hm.asp" target="_blank">Headstone, Markers and Medallions</a> page for more details.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>Deceased Veterans discharged under honorable conditions and members of the U.S. Armed Forces who died on active duty are eligible for a government headstone or marker. A veteran discharged under other than honorable conditions may be eligible.</p>

<p>A copy of the Veteran's discharge certificate or other official documents for proof of military service are required. Their service must have met one of the following conditions:</p>

<ul>
	<li>They served as an enlisted person after Sept. 7, 1980, or as an officer after Oct. 16, 1981, for a minimum of 24 consecutive months, or</li>
	<li>They completed their service under special circumstances, like death on active duty.</li>
</ul>

<p>For eligible Veterans who died <em>before</em> Nov. 1, 1990, by law, VA may only furnish a headstone or marker if the grave is unmarked. VA can't provide a medallion. For eligible Veterans who died <em>on or after</em> Nov. 1, 1990, the grave isnt required to be unmarked.</p>

<p>When the grave is already marked, you may apply for one of the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>A traditional headstone or marker, or</li>
	<li>A medallion to fasten to an existing privately bought headstone or marker.</li>
</ul>

<p>VA furnishes headstones and markers for eligible Veterans' spouses and dependents buried or memorialized in a national, military post or base, or state Veterans cemetery. Spouses and dependents buried in a private cemetery are not eligible.</p>

<p>Veterans whose only active duty service was for training while in the National Guard or Reserves are not eligible. A Veteran who died under special circumstances, like death while on duty or as a result of training, may qualify.</p>

<p>People with 20 years of service in the National Guard or Reserves who are entitled to retired pay are eligible. You must send a copy of the <em>Reserve Retirement Eligibility Benefits Letter</em> with the application. National Guard or Reserves who served in active duty (other than for training) also qualify. They do not need to be eligible for retiree pay.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>Please read all of the instructions on the application form carefully. It should take about 15 minutes to complete the form, when military documents are available.</p>

<p>You may complete <a href="http://www.va.gov/vaforms/va/pdf/VA40-1330.pdf" target="_blank">VA Form 40-1330</a>, <em>Claim for Standard Government Headstone or Marker </em>online and print for signatures. Or you may print and fill out a blank form.</p>

<p>You must have proof of honorable active-duty military service. Review this list of <a href="http://www.cem.va.gov/CEM/hmm/discharge_documents.asp" target="_blank">Veterans military discharge documents</a> to see if your documents support the application.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>For more help or questions about inscriptions, call our Applicant Assistance Division:</p>

<ul>
	<li>1-800-697-6947</li>
</ul>

<p>To learn more, visit the<a href="http://www.cem.va.gov/" target="_blank">National Cemetery Administration</a>website.</p>

<p>To apply for other benefits and view your benefit status, open a free eBenefits Premium account. eBenefits is a one-stop resource for Department of Defense (DoD) and VA benefits and services. Veterans, Servicemembers, and their families may open eBenefits accounts.</p>

<p>With a Premium account you can handle self-service actions like the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Check claim status.</li>
	<li>Handle GI Bill enrollment.</li>
	<li>Get copies of civil service preference letters, DD214, and other personal information.</li>
</ul>

<p>Visit <a href="http://www.ebenefits.va.gov/" target="_blank">eBenefits</a> to learn more or register for an account.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">VA - Burial Benefits - Veteran and Dependent Burial in VA National Cemeteries</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Department of Veterans Affairs' (VA) National Cemetery Administration honors Veterans with a final resting place and lasting memorials that pay tribute to their... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="VA - Burial Benefits - Veteran and Dependent Burial in VA National Cemeteries" data-agency="U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Department of Veterans Affairs' (VA) National Cemetery Administration honors Veterans with a final resting place and lasting memorials that pay tribute to their service to our nation.<br />
<br />
The NCA maintains 134 national cemeteries in 40 states and Puerto Rico. We also maintain 33 soldiers lots and monument sites. Please note that not every state has a VA national cemetery.<br />
<br />
Burial benefits include, at no cost to the family:</p>

<ul>
	<li>A gravesite in any of our open cemeteries with available space.</li>
	<li>Opening and closing of the grave.</li>
	<li>Perpetual care.</li>
	<li>A government headstone or marker.</li>
	<li>A burial flag.</li>
	<li>A Presidential Memorial Certificate (PMC).</li>
</ul>

<p>Some Veterans may also qualify for <a href="https://www.benefits.va.gov/BENEFITS/factsheets/burials/Burial.pdf" target="_blank">VA Burial Allowances</a>.</p>

<p>National cemeteries can also bury and inurn created remains in in the same manner and with the same honors as casket remains.<br />
<br />
Burial benefits for eligible spouses and dependents include, at no cost to the family:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Burial with the Veteran.</li>
	<li>Perpetual care of the interment site.</li>
	<li>The spouses or dependent's name and the date of birth and death inscribed on the Veteran's headstone.</li>
</ul>

<p>We can also bury eligible spouses and dependents even if they die before the Veteran.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>Deceased Veterans discharged under honorable conditions and any member of the U.S. Armed Forces who died on active duty may be eligible for burial in a national cemetery.<br />
<br />
Veterans whose only active duty service was for training while in the National Guard or Reserves are not eligible, unless there are special circumstances, like death while on duty or as a result of training.<br />
<br />
National Guard and Reserves who are entitled to retired pay qualify. You must send a copy of the <em>Reserve Retirement Eligibility Benefits Letter</em> with the application. National Guard or Reserves who served in active duty (other than for training) also qualify. They do not need to be eligible for retiree pay.<br />
<br />
Commissioned Officers of the Public Health Service (PHS) and National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) qualify as active duty members and Veterans once discharged.<br />
<br />
Any Veteran discharged from the U.S. Armed Forces under conditions other than dishonorable is eligible for a government-furnished headstone or marker.</p>

<p>Service must have been one of the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>They served as an enlisted person after Sept. 7, 1980, or as an officer after Oct. 16, 1981, for a minimum of 24 consecutive months, or</li>
	<li>They completed their service under special circumstances, like death on active.</li>
</ul>

<p>To get VA benefits and services, the Veteran or Servicemember's discharge or service must be other than dishonorable.</p>

<p>Some may qualify for benefits, pending a review by VA, who have other than an honorable discharge.<br />
<br />
You can visit the <a href="https://www.cem.va.gov/cem/burial_benefits/eligible.asp" target="_blank">Eligibility</a> page for more details.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>To learn more, visit the <a href="https://www.cem.va.gov/cem/burial_benefits/" target="_blank">National Cemetery Administration Burial Benefits</a> page.<br />
<br />
For a list of national cemeteries by state, see the <a href="https://www.cem.va.gov/cem/cems/listcem.asp" target="_blank">Department of Veterans Affairs Cemetery Listing</a>.</p>

<p>You cant make requests for burial in a VA national cemetery online. Funeral homes assisting families can contact the National Cemetery Scheduling Office to arrange for burial or inurnment and a committal service.</p>

<p>To schedule a burial, fax the Veterans discharge papers to the <a href="https://www.cem.va.gov/CEM/burial_benefits/need.asp" target="_blank">National Cemetery Scheduling Office</a> at 1-866-900-6417 and follow up with a phone call to 1-800-535-1117.</p>

<p>Direct contact with a Veteran's family is usually not necessary until the family arrives at the cemetery for the committal service.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Visit the<a href="https://iris.custhelp.com/" name="U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs || U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs" target="_blank"> Inquify Routing &amp; Information System (IRIS)</a> to search <strong>Frequently Asked Questions</strong>or<strong>Ask</strong><strong> a </strong><strong>Question</strong>online.</li>
	<li>Call 1-800-827-1000 or TDD 1-800-829-4833.</li>
</ul>

<p>To apply for other benefits and view your benefit status, open a free eBenefits Premium Account. eBenefits is a one-stop resource for Department of Defense (DOD) and VA benefits and services. Veterans, Servicemembers, and their families may open eBenefits accounts.</p>

<p>With a Premium Account you can handle self-service actions like the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Check claim status</li>
	<li>Handle GI Bill enrollment.</li>
	<li>Get copies of civil service preference letters, DD214, and other personal information</li>
</ul>

<p>To learn more and register for an account, visit <a href="https://www.ebenefits.va.gov" target="_blank">eBenefits</a>.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">Emergency Farm Loans</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Agriculture</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>Have the President or Secretary of Agriculture declared or designated your area as a disaster or quarantine area? 

If so,... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Emergency Farm Loans" data-agency="U.S. Department of Agriculture">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p><strong><em>Have the President or Secretary of Agriculture declared or designated your area as a disaster or quarantine area? </em></strong></p>

<p><strong><em>If so, do you own or operate a farm or ranch in the primary or an adjoining county?</em></strong></p>

<p>If you can answer yes to both of these questions, the U.S. Department of Agriculture's Farm Service Agency (USDA FSA) offers emergency loans that may help you.</p>

<p>Emergency loan funds may be used to:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Restore or replace essential property.</li>
	<li>Pay all or part of production costs for the disaster year.</li>
	<li>Pay essential family living expenses.</li>
	<li>Reorganize the farming operation.</li>
	<li>Refinance certain debts.</li>
</ul>

<p>You may borrow up to 100 percent of your actual production or physical losses, up to a maximum of $500,000. Production losses must exceed 30 percent; other terms and conditions apply. View the <a href="https://www.fsa.usda.gov/Assets/USDA-FSA-Public/usdafiles/FactSheets/2017/emergency_loan_program_oct2017.pdf" target="_blank">Emergency Loan Program</a> (PDF, 232 KB) fact sheet for details.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>You may get an emergency loan if youre a farmer or rancher who meets the conditions below:</p>

<ul>
	<li>You own or operate land in a county declared by the President or designated by the Secretary of Agriculture as a primary disaster or quarantine area. A disaster designation by the FSA administrator authorizes emergency loan assistance for physical losses only in the named and all adjoining counties.</li>
	<li>You are an established family farm operator and has sufficient farming or ranching experience.</li>
	<li>You are a U.S. citizen or permanent resident.</li>
	<li>You have at least a 30 percent loss in crop production or a physical loss to livestock, livestock products, real estate, or chattel property.</li>
	<li>You have an acceptable credit history.</li>
	<li>You are not able to get credit from commercial sources.</li>
	<li>You can provide collateral to secure the loan.</li>
	<li>You have repayment ability.</li>
</ul>

<p>Other terms and conditions may apply.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>To apply for an emergency loan, you must submit form <a href="http://forms.sc.egov.usda.gov/efcommon/eFileServices/eForms/FSA2001.PDF" target="_blank">FSA-2001, Request for Direct Loan Assistance</a> (PDF, 586 KB) and all required documentation to your local USDA Service Center or FSA County Office.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>You may use the <a href="http://offices.sc.egov.usda.gov/locator/app" target="_blank">USDA Service Center Locator</a> to find your local FSA County Office.</p>

<p>To learn more about this program and how to apply, visit FSAs <a href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/programs-and-services/farm-loan-programs/emergency-farm-loans/index" target="_blank">Emergency Farm Loans</a> page.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">Business and Industry Loans</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Agriculture</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Business &amp; Industry (B&amp;I) Guaranteed Loan Program helps boost the existing private credit structure of rural communities. The program does this through loan... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Business and Industry Loans" data-agency="U.S. Department of Agriculture">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Business &amp; Industry (B&amp;I) Guaranteed Loan Program helps boost the existing private credit structure of rural communities. The program does this through loan guarantees for rural businesses. These guarantees then allow private lenders to extend more credit than they would normally be able to.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p><strong>What kind of borrower may a lender request a guarantee for?</strong></p>

<ul>
	<li>For-profit businesses</li>
	<li>Nonprofits and cooperatives</li>
	<li>Federally recognized tribes</li>
	<li>Public bodies</li>
	<li>Individuals</li>
</ul>

<p><strong>How may I use the funds?</strong></p>

<p>Uses may include:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Business repair, modernization, or development.</li>
	<li>Purchase and development of land, easements, or buildings.</li>
	<li>Purchase of equipment, supplies, or inventory.</li>
	<li>Debt refinancing that creates new jobs and meets other conditions.</li>
	<li>Business and industrial acquisitions that keeps a business from closing, or saves or creates jobs.</li>
</ul>

<p><strong>Are there restrictions on the borrower?</strong></p>

<ul>
	<li>Government or military employees may not own more than 20%.</li>
	<li>U.S. citizens or legal permanent residents must hold majority ownership.</li>
</ul>

<p><strong>What is an eligible area?</strong></p>

<ul>
	<li>Rural areas outside a city or town with a population under 50,000.</li>
	<li>Projects in an eligible rural area may have a borrower based in a larger city.</li>
	<li>Lenders may be located anywhere.</li>
</ul>

<p>You can check the <a href="http://eligibility.sc.egov.usda.gov/eligibility/welcomeAction.do?pageAction=RBSmenu&amp;NavKey=property@13" target="_blank">Rural Business Services</a> page to see if your address is in an eligible area.</p>

<p>Before filling out any forms, please speak to a Business Programs Specialist at a state office. This will help save you time.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>If you're a lender, you may apply year round through a local state office. If you'd like to borrow, talk with your lender about the program.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions or want to learn more, contact your local <a href="http://www.rd.usda.gov/contact-us/state-offices" target="_blank">state office</a>. You may also visit the <a href="http://www.rd.usda.gov/programs-services/business-industry-loan-guarantees" target="_blank">Business &amp; Industry Loan Guarantees</a> page for more details.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">American Job Centers Network</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Labor</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The American Job Center network helps job seekers as well as businesses. The network helps businesses find qualified workers and provides free help to job seekers for a... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="American Job Centers Network" data-agency="U.S. Department of Labor">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The American Job Center network helps job seekers as well as businesses. The network helps businesses find qualified workers and provides free help to job seekers for a variety of career and employment-related needs. There are nearly 2,500 American Job Centers (or AJCs) located across the U.S.</p>

<p><strong>How can an American Job Center help me? </strong></p>

<p>AJCs can help you look for work and offer job search workshops, free computer access, and more. Services vary by location but may include the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Resource rooms with phones, free Internet, and resume writing tools.</li>
	<li>Employment plan development.</li>
	<li>Job training services.</li>
	<li>Job search help.</li>
	<li>Career counseling and practice interviewing.</li>
	<li>Skills testing.</li>
	<li>Labor market and employer information.</li>
	<li>Employment workshops.</li>
	<li>Supportive services (which may include information about SNAP, financial assistance, Medicaid, child care, emergency funds, and other benefits.</li>
	<li>Hiring events and business service information.</li>
	<li>Accessibility and special accommodations for people with disabilities.</li>
	<li>Referrals to community resources, other agencies, and more.</li>
	<li>Help using CareerOneStop's <a href="http://www.careeronestop.org/ReEmployment" target="_blank">Worker ReEmployment</a> website for laid-off workers.</li>
	<li>Access to your states job bank or CareerOneStops national <a href="http://www.careeronestop.org/JobSearch/job-search.aspx" target="_blank">Job Finder</a>.</li>
	<li>Unemployment insurance info.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>AJCs help people search for jobs, find training, and answer other employment-related questions.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>Many services in an AJC do not require an application and are self-service. Certain specialized services may require an application. Check with your local center for details.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>Please visit the CareerOneStop <a href="http://www.careeronestop.org/localhelp/local-help.aspx" target="_blank">Find Local Help</a> page to learn more about local programs and services. To find a center near you, enter your location and search under the <em>Find an American Job Center</em> section.</p>

<p>You may also call the Employment and Training Helpline.</p>

	<li>1-877-US2-JOBS (1-877-872-5627)</li>

<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">U.S. Postal Service (USPS) Change of Address</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Postal Service</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The USPS Change of Address lets you enter an order to forward your mail to a new address. This can be helpful if you need to relocate after a... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="U.S. Postal Service (USPS) Change of Address" data-agency="U.S. Postal Service">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The USPS Change of Address lets you enter an order to forward your mail to a new address. This can be helpful if you need to relocate after a disaster.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>Anyone can use this feature to change their address and forward their mail. You can request a change for both permanent as well as temporary moves.</p>

<p>We can forward mail for a minimum length of 15 days. The initial forwarding period is restricted to six months. You may extend this service up to one year.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>There are two ways you can change your address:</p>

<ol>
	<li>Visit the <a href="https://moversguide.usps.com/icoa/home/icoa-main-flow.do?execution=e1s1&amp;_flowId=icoa-main-flow&amp;referral=MG82" target="_blank">Official USPS Change of Address</a> page to submit the order.<br />
	<br />
	You must have both of the following for us to confirm your identity:
	<ul><br />
		<li>A valid credit or debit card. (We add a $1.00 charge to your account to verify.)</li>
		<li>A valid email address. (You get a confirmation message after you place the order.)</li>
	</ul>
	</li>
	<br />
	<li>Fill out and submit PS Form 3575, available at any U.S. Post Office. When you sign the form, you confirm that you are the person or a representative of the person we will be forwarding the mail to.<br />
	<br />
	You may then submit the form using one of the methods below:
	<ul><br />
		<li>Take or mail the form to any U.S. Post Office.</li>
		<li>Give it to any Postal Mail Carrier.</li>
	</ul>
	</li>
</ol>

<p>You can also <a href="https://managemymove.usps.com/coac/coacorrect-main-flow.do" target="_blank">view, update, or cancel an order</a> you have already submitted.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>To learn more, visit the <a href="https://www.usps.com/help/welcome.htm" target="_blank">USPS Help</a> page or call 1-800-ASK-USPS (275-8777).</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">Disaster Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program (D-SNAP) </h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Agriculture</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Disaster Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program (D-SNAP) gives food assistance to low-income households with food loss or damage caused by a natural... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Disaster Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program (D-SNAP) " data-agency="U.S. Department of Agriculture">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Disaster Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program (D-SNAP) gives food assistance to low-income households with food loss or damage caused by a natural disaster.</p>

<p>The U.S. Department of Agriculture's Food and Nutrition Service (USDA FNS) must approve states to operate D-SNAP in a disaster area. The President must declare Individual Assistance for the disaster area and your state must request FNS approval to operate D-SNAP.</p>

<p>If approved for D-SNAP benefits, you will get an Electronic Benefits Transfer (EBT) card to access them. You use it just like a debit card to buy food at most local grocery stores.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>Because of the unique needs of disaster survivors, D-SNAP uses different standards than normal SNAP. If you would not normally qualify for SNAP, you may qualify for D-SNAP if you had one of the disaster-related expenses below:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Home or business repairs</li>
	<li>Temporary shelter expenses</li>
	<li>Evacuation or relocation expenses</li>
	<li>Home or business protection</li>
	<li>Disaster-related personal injury, including funeral expenses</li>
	<li>Lost or no access to income due to the disaster, including reduced, terminated, or delayed receipt of income, for a large part of the benefit period</li>
	<li>In some cases, food loss after a disaster like flooding or power outages</li>
</ul>

<p>If youre a current SNAP client, you can request a supplement when your state operates a D-SNAP if you meet the conditions below:</p>

<ul>
	<li>You currently get benefits that are less than the monthly maximum, and</li>
	<li>You have losses from the disaster.</li>
</ul>

<p>The supplement brings your benefits up to the maximum for your household size. This way benefits are equal between D-SNAP and SNAP households after a disaster.</p>

<p>Current SNAP clients may also request replacement benefits for food that was lost in the disaster and bought with SNAP benefits. Just contact your local office.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>As a disaster survivor, you may apply for D-SNAP benefits at special sites in your community. Before the program begins, state agencies release information through local media and press. This can help you learn the location of application sites, their days of operation, and the eligibility requirements.</p>

<p>You can also view a list of <a href="http://www.fns.usda.gov/snap/contact_info/hotlines.htm" target="_blank">state SNAP hotlines</a> to call for other benefit details.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>To learn more, read the <a href="http://www.fns.usda.gov/sites/default/files/D-SNAP_Disaster.pdf" target="_blank">D-SNAP Fact Sheet</a> (PDF, 143KB).</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">Livestock Indemnity Program (LIP)</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Agriculture</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Livestock Indemnity Program (LIP) offers payments to livestock producers for livestock deaths in excess of normal mortality caused by bad weather. LIP also covers... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Livestock Indemnity Program (LIP)" data-agency="U.S. Department of Agriculture">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Livestock Indemnity Program (LIP) offers payments to livestock producers for livestock deaths in excess of normal mortality caused by bad weather. LIP also covers attacks by animals reintroduced into the wild by the federal government or protected by federal law. This includes attacks by wolves and birds.</p>

<p>LIP payments equal 75 percent of the livestocks market value on the day before the date of death.</p>

<p>Visit the <a href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/programs-and-services/disaster-assistance-program/livestock-indemnity/index" target="_blank">LIP</a> page to get more details.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>To qualify, you must have legally owned the eligible livestock, poultry, or swine on the day they died, and they must:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Have died due to an eligible weather event on or after Oct. 1, 2011, and no later than 60 days from the end date of the event.</li>
	<li>Have been for commercial use in a farming operation on the day they died.</li>
	<li>Have died in the calendar year of requested benefits.</li>
</ul>

<p>Excludes wild, free-roaming animals, or pets or animals used for recreational purposes. This includes animals used for for hunting, roping, or show.</p>

<p>You must have had possession and control of the livestock and a written agreement with the livestock owner. The specific terms, conditions, and obligations of both parties must be set.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>To apply for payment, you must submit a notice of loss and an application at your local Farm Service Agency (FSA) office. You must submit the notice of loss the earlier of the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>30 days of when the loss of livestock is known, or</li>
	<li>30 days after the calendar year end of the loss year.</li>
</ul>

<p>If youre a contract grower, you must include a copy of the grower contract. The supporting documents you submit must also show the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Evidence of loss.</li>
	<li>Current physical location of livestock inventory.</li>
	<li>Location of the livestock at the time of death.</li>
</ul>

<p>Other terms and conditions may apply.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>To learn more, visit the <a href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/programs-and-services/disaster-assistance-program/index" target="_blank">Disaster Assistance Program</a> page or contact your local <a href="http://offices.sc.egov.usda.gov/locator/app?state=us&amp;agency=fsa" target="_blank">Farm Service Agency</a> office.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">Livestock Forage Disaster Program (LFP)</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Agriculture</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Livestock Forage Disaster Program (LFP) offers payments to eligible livestock producers with covered livestock. The payments help with grazing losses suffered on... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Livestock Forage Disaster Program (LFP)" data-agency="U.S. Department of Agriculture">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Livestock Forage Disaster Program (LFP) offers payments to eligible livestock producers with covered livestock. The payments help with grazing losses suffered on native or improved pastureland. This can be land with permanent or planted grazing cover. LFP also provides for livestock producers on rangeland managed by a federal agency, if the agency prohibits grazing on the land due to a qualifying fire.</p>

<p>Farm Service Agency (FSA) will calculate payments equal to 1, 3, 4 or 5 times the LFP monthly payment rate. The payment rate for drought is equal to 60 percent of the lessor of the monthly feed cost. They calculate this by using the normal carrying capacity of the grazing land.</p>

<p>View the <a href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/programs-and-services/disaster-assistance-program/livestock-forage/index" target="_blank">LFP</a> page to get more details.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>We calculate LFP payments based on the U.S. Drought Monitor rating for your county. If you suffered losses on eligible grazing or pasture land you own or lease, you may qualify for assistance.</p>

<p>The eligible livestock that would normally graze your land may include:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Alpacas, llamas</li>
	<li>Beef &amp; dairy cattle, beefalo, buffalo</li>
	<li>Deer, elk, reindeer</li>
	<li>Emus, Poultry</li>
	<li>Equine, goats, sheep, swine</li>
</ul>

<p>As a livestock producer you must:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Own, cash or share lease, or be a contract grower of eligible livestock during the 60 calendar days before the beginning date of a qualifying drought or fire.</li>
	<li>Provide pastureland or grazing land for eligible livestock, including cash-rented land that is either:
	<ol>
		<li>Physically located in an eligible county, or</li>
		<li>Managed by a federal agency that has prohibited you from grazing because of fire.</li>
	</ol>
	</li>
	<li>Certify that you have suffered a grazing loss because of qualifying drought or fire.</li>
	<li>File a timely acreage report for your loss claim.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>For grazing losses in 2016 and future calendar years, you must submit an application for payment. You must apply within 30 calendar days after the calendar year end of the loss year. Submit your application and all supporting documents to your local FSA office.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>To learn more, visit the <a href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/programs-and-services/disaster-assistance-program/index" target="_blank">Disaster Assistance Program</a> page or contact your local <a href="http://offices.sc.egov.usda.gov/locator/app?state=us&amp;agency=fsa" target="_blank">Farm Service Agency</a> office.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">Summer Food Service Program (SFSP) - Disaster Response </h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Agriculture</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Summer Food Service Program (SFSP) provides free, healthy meals to children from low-income families when school is not in session. After a disaster, state agencies,... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Summer Food Service Program (SFSP) - Disaster Response " data-agency="U.S. Department of Agriculture">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Summer Food Service Program (SFSP) provides free, healthy meals to children from low-income families when school is not in session. After a disaster, state agencies, food authorities, and sponsors may decide to open emergency program feeding sites when schools or daycare centers must stay closed.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>All children and teens (age 18 and under) who visit an approved SFSP feeding site can get free meals. Meals are also available for people with disabilities, over age 18, who participate in school programs for the mentally or physically disabled.</p>

<p>If a community is in need, the Food and Nutrition Service (FNS) may waive the rule to serve meals only in low-income areas. State agencies may also allow feeding sites to be set up in closed schools if buildings are unharmed by the disaster.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>All children (age 18 and under) can get free meals at an approved site. No application is required.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>To learn more, visit the <a href="http://www.fns.usda.gov/disaster-assistance" target="_blank">Food Assistance for Disaster Relief</a> page and read about Child Nutrition Programs.</p>

<p>If you need food help today, you may also call the National Hunger Hotline. Hotline staff can help you find food near where you live:</p>

<ul>
	<li>1-866-3-HUNGRY (1-866-348-6479)</li>
	<li>1-877-8-HAMBRE (1-877-842-6273) (en espaol)</li>
</ul>

<p>To find FNS state and regional contacts, visit the pages below:</p>

<ul>
	<li>State agencies: <a href="http://www.fns.usda.gov/sfsp/sfsp-contacts" target="_blank">SFSP Contacts</a></li>
	<li>Regional offices: <a href="http://www.fns.usda.gov/fns-regional-offices" target="_blank">FNS Regional Offices</a></li>
</ul>

<p>To find other FNS program contacts, visit the <a href="http://www.fns.usda.gov/contact-us" target="_blank">Contact Us</a> page.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">Tree Assistance Program (TAP)</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Agriculture</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Tree Assistance Program (TAP) provides payments to qualifying orchardists and nursery tree growers after a natural disaster. The funds may help you replant or... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Tree Assistance Program (TAP)" data-agency="U.S. Department of Agriculture">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Tree Assistance Program (TAP) provides payments to qualifying orchardists and nursery tree growers after a natural disaster. The funds may help you replant or rehabilitate eligible trees, bushes, and vines damaged by the disaster.</p>

<p>Payments are made based on the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>The lesser of 65% of the actual cost of replanting, in excess of 15% mortality, or</li>
	<li>50% of the actual cost of rehabilitation, in excess of 15% mortality, or both, or</li>
	<li>The maximum eligible amount allowed for the practice by FSA.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>Eligible trees, bushes, and vines are those that produce an annual commercial crop. Nursery trees include ornamental, fruit, nut, and Christmas trees. Trees used for pulp or timber are not eligible.</p>

<p>You must meet the terms below to qualify:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Have eligible losses caused by natural disaster.</li>
	<li>Have a mortality loss or damage in excess of 15% after adjustment for normal mortality or damage.</li>
	<li>Have been unable to prevent the loss through any reasonable measures.</li>
	<li>Owned the eligible trees, bushes, and vines at the time of the disaster, and</li>
	<li>Must replace trees, bushes, and vines within 12 months from the application approval date.</li>
</ul>

<p>For more details, visit the <a href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/programs-and-services/disaster-assistance-program/tree-assistance-program/index" target="_blank">Tree Assistance Program (TAP)</a> page.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>You must submit your application to the FSA office that maintains your farm records.</p>

<p>For losses incurred in and after calendar year 2015, you must submit your application within one of the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>90 days of the disaster, or</li>
	<li>90 days of the date when you find the loss.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>To learn more, visit the <a href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/programs-and-services/disaster-assistance-program/index" target="_blank">Disaster Assistance Program</a> page or contact your local <a href="http://offices.sc.egov.usda.gov/locator/app?state=us&amp;agency=fsa" target="_blank">Farm Service Agency</a> office.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">Emergency Assistance for Livestock, Honeybees, and Farm-raised Fish Program (ELAP)</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Agriculture</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Emergency Assistance for Livestock, Honeybees, and Farm-Raised Fish Program (ELAP) provides $20 million each fiscal year in emergency assistance to eligible producers.... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Emergency Assistance for Livestock, Honeybees, and Farm-raised Fish Program (ELAP)" data-agency="U.S. Department of Agriculture">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Emergency Assistance for Livestock, Honeybees, and Farm-Raised Fish Program (ELAP) provides $20 million each fiscal year in emergency assistance to eligible producers. The funds cover losses due to eligible weather or other events, like blizzards, disease (including cattle tick fever), water shortages, and wildfires.</p>

<p>ELAP covers losses that the 2014 Farm Bill doesnt cover under other Disaster Assistance Programs. These other programs include the <a href="https://www.disasterassistance.gov/get-assistance/forms-of-assistance/5801" target="_self">Livestock Forage Disaster Program</a> (LFP) and the <a href="https://www.disasterassistance.gov/get-assistance/forms-of-assistance/5800" target="_self">Livestock Indemnity Program</a> (LIP).</p>

<p>ELAP covers:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Livestock death losses.</li>
	<li>The costs of hauling water to livestock.</li>
	<li>Livestock feed and grazing losses.</li>
	<li>The cost of gathering and treating livestock for cattle tick fever.</li>
	<li>Honeybee colony and hive losses.</li>
	<li>Honeybee feed losses.</li>
	<li>Farm-raised fish death and feed losses.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>Program requirements vary depending on the type of loss and whether livestock, honey bees, or farm-raised fish are affected.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>For more details and to find out how to apply, you can read the individual fact sheets found on the <a href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/programs-and-services/disaster-assistance-program/emergency-assist-for-livestock-honey-bees-fish/index" target="_blank">ELAP</a> page. You may also contact your local USDA Service Center or FSA office.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>To learn more, visit the <a href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/programs-and-services/disaster-assistance-program/index" target="_blank">Disaster Assistance Program</a> page or contact your local <a href="http://offices.sc.egov.usda.gov/locator/app?state=us&amp;agency=fsa" target="_blank">Farm Service Agency</a> office.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">VA-Guaranteed Home Loan Program</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) Home Loan Guaranty program may be able to help eligible Servicemembers, Veterans, Reservists, National Guard members, and certain... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="VA-Guaranteed Home Loan Program" data-agency="U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) Home Loan Guaranty program may be able to help eligible Servicemembers, Veterans, Reservists, National Guard members, and certain surviving spouses get, keep, or adapt a home. It may also be able to help you refinance your loan.</p>

<p>Visit the <a href="http://www.benefits.va.gov/homeloans/" target="_blank">Home Loans</a> page to learn more.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>VA does not have the authority to take a second-lien position on a property. In the case of disaster, the Secretary may guarantee a loan whether or not it is subordinate to a higher lien through a public entity providing disaster assistance.</p>

<p>You may qualify for a VA-guaranteed loan if you are a(n):</p>

<ul>
	<li>Eligible Veteran or Servicemember.</li>
	<li>Current Reserve or National Guard member (after 6 years of creditable service).</li>
	<li>Certain surviving spouse.</li>
</ul>

<p>Commissioned Officers of the Public Health Service (PHS) and National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) qualify as active duty members and Veterans once discharged.</p>

<p>You or your spouse must certify occupancy for the property. A dependent child of an active duty Servicemember may also satisfy the occupancy requirement.</p>

<p>Length-of-service requirements may apply.</p>

<p>To get VA benefits, your discharge or service must be under honorable conditions; Reserve and National Guard members must have an honorable discharge.</p>

<p>Sometimes those with undesirable, bad conduct, and other types of dishonorable discharges may qualify for VA benefits. This depends on a determination by VA. You can review the <a href="http://benefits.va.gov/HOMELOANS/purchaseco_eligibility.asp" target="_blank">eligibility</a> page to learn more.</p>

<p><strong>Loan Terms:</strong></p>

<p>Under the VA-guaranteed Home Loan program, VA does not make the loan to you. Private-sector lenders make the loans. The guaranty amount is what VA would pay a lender should your loan go into foreclosure, deed-in-lieu, or short-sale.</p>

<p>There is no maximum loan amount, only a maximum guaranty amount, set by law. Due to secondary market requirements, lenders may require that the VA guaranty, plus any down payment made by you, total 25 percent of the loan amount. This means the "loan limit is an amount equal to four times VA's maximum guaranty.</p>

<ul>
	<li>Loans for the loan limit or less may be available with no down payment.</li>
	<li>Loans for more than the loan limit may require a down payment.</li>
</ul>

<p>VA's maximum guaranty amounts are set annually. The amounts may vary depending on the size of the loan and location of the property.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>To apply, you will need a valid Certificate of Eligibility (COE). There are several ways to get one:</p>

<ul>
	<li>You may be able to get a COE through eBenefits.</li>
	<li>If you're not able to get your COE through eBenefits, check with your lender. In most cases, they will be able to get a COE for you using the Automated Certificate of Eligibility (ACE) program.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Go to the <a href="https://iris.custhelp.com/app/answers/detail/a_id/1080" target="_blank">Inquiry Routing and Information System</a> (IRIS) website to search Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs) or ask a question.</li>
	<li>For detailed questions, contact a <a href="http://www.benefits.va.gov/homeloans/contact_rlc_info.asp" target="_blank">Regional Loan Center</a>.</li>
</ul>

<p>To apply for other benefits and view your benefit status, open a free eBenefits Premium account. eBenefits is a one-stop resource for Department of Defense (DoD) and VA benefits and services. Veterans, Servicemembers, and their families may open eBenefits accounts.</p>

<p>With a Premium account you can handle self-service actions like the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Check claim status.</li>
	<li>Handle GI Bill enrollment.</li>
	<li>Get copies of civil service preference letters, DD214, and other personal information.</li>
</ul>

<p>Visit <a href="http://www.ebenefits.va.gov/" target="_blank">eBenefits</a> to learn more and register for an account.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">Specially Adapted Housing Grant </h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>If you're a Veteran or Servicemember with a serious service-connected disability, you may be able to get a housing grant from Veterans Affairs (VA).

Two grant... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Specially Adapted Housing Grant " data-agency="U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>If you're a Veteran or Servicemember with a serious service-connected disability, you may be able to get a housing grant from Veterans Affairs (VA).</p>

<p>Two grant programs exist: the Specially Adapted Housing (SAH) grant and the Special Housing Adaptation (SHA) grant. You may use a grant to buy or build an adapted home, or modify an existing home to meet your needs. These grants can help you live independently in a barrier-free setting.</p>

<p>You may use an SAH grant for one of the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Build a specially adapted home on land you already own or land you are buying.</li>
	<li>Remodel an existing home if it can be adapted to meet your needs.</li>
	<li>Apply the grant to the mortgage balance of an adapted home not bought using VA grant funds.</li>
</ul>

<p>You may use an SHA grant for one of the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Adapt the home you currently live in, already owned by you or a family member.</li>
	<li>Adapt a home for you to live in, being bought by you or a family member.</li>
	<li>Help you buy a home that's already adapted for you to live in.</li>
</ul>

<p>Under either program, you may also be able to get a Temporary Residence Adaptation (TRA) grant. You may use this grant if you are or will temporarily live in a home owned by a family member; certain limits apply.</p>

<p>Visit <a href="http://www.benefits.va.gov/homeloans/adaptedhousing.asp" target="_blank">Housing Grants for Disabled Veterans</a> to learn more.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>The SAH and SHA grants are for Veterans and Servicemembers with certain permanent and total service-connected disabilities.</p>

<p>For the SAH grant, your disability may include:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Loss or loss of use of both legs, or</li>
	<li>Loss or loss of use of both arms, or</li>
	<li>Blindness in both eyes having only light perception, plus loss or loss of use of one leg, or</li>
	<li>The loss or loss of use of one lower leg together with residuals of organic disease or injury, or</li>
	<li>The loss or loss of use of one leg together with the loss or loss of use of one arm, or</li>
	<li>Certain severe burns, or</li>
	<li>The loss or loss of use of one or more lower limbs due to service on or after September 11, 2001. This must affect your balance or movement, and hinder walking without the aid of braces, crutches, canes, or a wheelchair. This provision expires September 30, 2018.</li>
</ul>

<p>For the SHA grant, your disability may include:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Blindness in both eyes with 20/200 vision or less, or</li>
	<li>Loss or loss of use of both hands, or</li>
	<li>Certain severe burn injuries, or</li>
	<li>Certain severe respiratory injuries.</li>
</ul>

<p>You have a maximum of three grants uses up to the maximum dollar limit.</p>

<p>If you get an SAH grant, you may also qualify for Veterans Mortgage Life Insurance. This provides coverage on home mortgages up to $200,000. You can go to <a href="http://www.benefits.gov/benefits/benefit-details/587" target="_blank">Veterans Mortgage Life Insurance (VMLI)</a> to learn more.</p>

<p>To get VA benefits, your discharge or service must be other than dishonorable (e.g., honorable, under honorable conditions, general); Reserve and National Guard members must have an honorable discharge.</p>

<p>Sometimes those with undesirable, bad conduct, and other types of dishonorable discharges may qualify for VA benefits. This depends on a determination by VA.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>To apply, use <a href="http://www.vba.va.gov/pubs/forms/VBA-26-4555-ARE.pdf" target="_blank">VA Form 26-4555</a> (PDF, 400 KB), <em>Veteran's Application In Acquiring Specially Adapted Housing or Special Home Adaptation Grant</em> and mail it to your closest <a href="http://www.benefits.va.gov/HOMELOANS/contact_rlc_info.asp" target="_blank">Regional Loan Center</a>.</p>

<p>You may also visit a local <a href="http://www.va.gov/directory/guide/home.asp" target="_blank">VA regional office</a> or call 1-800-827-1000.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>Have questions or need more information? You may email an SAH staff member at <a href="mailto:sahinfo.vbaco@va.gov">sahinfo.vbaco@va.gov</a> or call 1-877-827-3702.</p>

<p>You may also get information through the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Call 1-877-222-VETS (8387)</li>
	<li>TTY 1-800-829-4833</li>
	<li>Go to the <a href="https://iris.custhelp.com/" target="_blank">Inquiry Routing &amp; Information System</a> (IRIS) website to search Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs) or ask a question.</li>
</ul>

<p>To apply for other benefits and view your status, open a free eBenefits Premium account. eBenefits is a one-stop resource for Department of Defense (DoD) and VA benefits and services. Veterans, Servicemembers, and their families may open eBenefits accounts.</p>

<p>With a Premium account you can handle self-service actions like the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Check claim status.</li>
	<li>Handle GI Bill enrollment.</li>
	<li>Get copies of civil service preference letters, DD214, and other personal information.</li>
</ul>

<p>Visit <a href="http://www.ebenefits.va.gov/" target="_blank">eBenefits</a> to learn more and register for an account.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">Loan Management </h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>If you're a Veteran or Servicemember with a VA-guaranteed loan, the Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) has a network of Regional Loan Centers that can offer advice and... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Loan Management " data-agency="U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>If you're a Veteran or Servicemember with a VA-guaranteed loan, the Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) has a network of Regional Loan Centers that can offer advice and guidance during times of financial hardship.</p>

<p>Visit the <a href="http://www.benefits.va.gov/homeloans/" target="_blank">Home Loans</a> page or call 1-877-827-3702 to speak with a VA Loan Technician.</p>

<p>Unlike a VA-guaranteed home loan, VA does not have the authority to act on your behalf for conventional loans. You must contact your mortgage servicer as quickly as possible when faced with financial hardship.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>VA does not have the authority to take a second-lien position on a property. In the case of disaster, the Secretary may guarantee a loan whether or not it is subordinate to a higher lien through a public entity providing disaster assistance.</p>

<p>You may qualify for VA-guaranteed loan if you are a(n):</p>

<ul>
	<li>Eligible Veteran or Servicemember.</li>
	<li>Current Reserve or National Guard member (after 6 creditable years of service).</li>
	<li>Certain surviving spouse.</li>
</ul>

<p>VA deems Commissioned Officers of the Public Health Service (PHS) and National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) active duty members and Veterans once discharged.</p>

<p>Length-of-service requirements may apply.</p>

<p><strong>Loan Terms:</strong></p>

<p>The mortgage servicer has the main responsibility of working to resolve the default. When VA deems other information or action is needed, we initiate contact with you to:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Offer financial counseling,</li>
	<li>Discuss the loss mitigation options considered, and</li>
	<li>Sometimes serve as an intermediary between you and your mortgage servicer to negotiate a resolution.</li>
</ul>

<p>VA then helps the servicer and you arrange a loss mitigation option, like one of those noted below:</p>

<ul>
	<li><strong>Repayment Plan</strong>  You pay a regular payment plus part of the missed payments each month until you bring the loan current.</li>
	<li><strong>Special Forbearance</strong>  The servicer agrees not to start foreclosure to allow you time to repay the missed payments, like if you're waiting for a tax refund.</li>
	<li><strong>Time to arrange a private sale</strong>  The servicer agrees to delay foreclosure to allow a sale to close if it will pay off the loan.</li>
	<li><strong>Loan Modification</strong>  You get a fresh start by adding the missed payments to the loan balance and creating a new payment schedule.</li>
	<li><strong>Refunding</strong>  VA can consider refunding (buying) the loan and modifying it to make the payments easier for you to afford.</li>
	<li><strong>Short Sale</strong>  You sell your home for less than what you owe and VA pays the difference, up to the maximum guaranty on the loan.</li>
	<li><strong>Deed-in-Lieu of Foreclosure</strong>  You voluntarily deed the property to the servicer to avoid foreclosure and VA pays the difference between the payoff and the net property value.</li>
</ul>

<p>Read the <a href="http://www.benefits.va.gov/homeloans/documents/docs/foreclosure_avoidance_fact_sheet.pdf" target="_blank">Delinquency Assistance</a> (PDF, 94 KB) fact sheet to learn more. You may also read <a href="http://www.benefits.va.gov/homeloans/documents/docs/va_policy_regarding_natural_disasters.pdf" target="_blank">VA Guidance on Natural Disasters</a> (PDF, 146 KB).</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>VA offers loss mitigation help to all Veterans with a VA-guaranteed loan. For Veterans without a VA-guaranteed loan, we can offer financial counseling, but have no legal standing to act directly with the mortgage loan servicer on your behalf.</p>

<p>Call 1-877-827-3702 for home loan assistance.</p>

<p>Visit the <a href="http://www.benefits.va.gov/homeloans/" target="_blank">Home Loans</a> page to find more information.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Go to the <a href="https://iris.custhelp.com/" target="_blank">Inquiry Routing and Information System</a> (IRIS) to search Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs) or ask a question.</li>
	<li>For more detailed questions, contact a <a href="http://www.benefits.va.gov/homeloans/contact_rlc_info.asp" target="_blank">Regional Loan Center</a>.</li>
</ul>

<p>To apply for other benefits and view your status, open a free eBenefits Premium account. eBenefits is a one-stop resource for Department of Defense (DoD) and VA benefits and services. Veterans, Servicemembers, and their families may open eBenefits accounts.</p>

<p>With a Premium account you can handle self-service actions like the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Check claim status.</li>
	<li>Handle GI Bill enrollment.</li>
	<li>Get copies of civil service preference letters, DD214, and other personal information.</li>
</ul>

<p>Visit <a href="http://www.ebenefits.va.gov/" target="_blank">eBenefits</a> to learn more or register for an account.</p>

<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">FEMA Individuals and Households Program (IHP) - Housing Assistance</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Homeland Security/FEMA</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>Housing Assistance under FEMAs Individuals and Households Program (IHP) can provide financial help and direct services after a disaster. The program provides money, if... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="FEMA Individuals and Households Program (IHP) - Housing Assistance" data-agency="U.S. Department of Homeland Security/FEMA">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>Housing Assistance under FEMAs Individuals and Households Program (IHP) can provide financial help and direct services after a disaster. The program provides money, if you qualify, for necessary housing-related expenses and serious needs caused by the disaster.</p>

<p>Housing assistance under IHP includes the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Lodging expense reimbursement for short-term stays.</li>
	<li>Rental Assistance for temporary housing.</li>
	<li>Direct Temporary Housing Assistance, which may include:
	<ul>
		<li>Multi-family lease and repair</li>
		<li>Direct lease</li>
		<li>Recreation vehicle (RV)</li>
		<li>Manufactured housing unit (MHU)</li>
	</ul>
	</li>
	<li>Repair or replacement of primary home.</li>
	<li>Semi-permanent or permanent housing construction.</li>
</ul>

<p>Read the <a href="http://www.fema.gov/media-library/assets/documents/24945" target="_blank">Individuals and Households Program Fact Sheet</a> (PDF, 132 KB) for more details.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>You must meet all of the following requirements to qualify:</p>

<ul>
	<li>You have losses in a presidentially declared disaster area.</li>
	<li>You have no insurance or have filed an insurance claim, but the damage for all of your losses isn't covered.</li>
	<li>You or someone who lives with you is a U.S. citizen, a non-citizen national, or a qualified alien.</li>
	<li>The affected home is your primary home.</li>
	<li>You can't access your home or your home requires repairs because of disaster damage.</li>
</ul>

<p>Certain conditions and limitations apply.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>To start an application, click <a href="/DAC/govBenefitReceiver.do?gbsessionid=0&amp;action=RI&amp;langcode=EN" target="_blank" title="Start Registration">Apply Online</a>.</p>

<p>If you have questions or prefer to apply by phone, you may call the FEMA Helpline at one of the program contact numbers below.</p>

<p>You can also visit a local Disaster Recovery Center (DRC) for help. Use the <a href="https://egateway.fema.gov/ESF6/DRCLocator" target="_blank">DRC Locator</a> to find a center near you.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions or want to apply by phone, call:</p>

<ul>
	<li>1-800-621-FEMA (3362)</li>
	<li>TTY 1-800-462-7585</li>
	<li>711 and VRS 1-800-621-3362</li>
</ul>

The program provides money, if you qualify, for necessary expenses and serious needs caused by the disaster.</p>

<p>Other needs assistance under IHP includes the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Personal property</li>
	<li>Childcare</li>
	<li>Medical and dental expenses</li>
	<li>Funeral and burial costs</li>
	<li>Transportation</li>
	<li>Moving and storage</li>
	<li>Miscellaneous and other expenses</li>
	<li>Critical needs assistance</li>
	<li>Group flood insurance program</li>
</ul>

<p>Read the <a href="http://www.fema.gov/media-library/assets/documents/24945" target="_blank">Individuals and Households Program Fact Sheet</a> (PDF, 132 KB) for more details.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>You must meet all of the following requirements to qualify:</p>

<ul>
	<li>You have losses in a presidentially declared disaster area.</li>
	<li>You have no insurance or have filed an insurance claim, but the damage for all of your losses isn't covered.</li>
	<li>You or someone who lives with you is a U.S. citizen, a non-citizen national, or a qualified alien.</li>
	<li>You have necessary expenses or serious needs because of the disaster.</li>
	<li>You have accepted help from all other available sources, like insurance or Small Business Administration (SBA) disaster loans.</li>
</ul>

<p>Certain conditions and limitations apply</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>To start an application, click <a href="/DAC/govBenefitReceiver.do?gbsessionid=0&amp;langcode=EN&amp;action=RI" target="_blank" title="Start Registration">Apply Online</a>. If youve already submitted an application for IHP, you dont need to do a separate one for ONA.</p>

<p>If you have questions or prefer to apply by phone, you may call the FEMA Helpline at one of the program contact numbers below.</p>

<p>You can also visit a local Disaster Recovery Center (DRC) for help. Use the <a href="https://egateway.fema.gov/ESF6/DRCLocator" target="_blank">DRC Locator</a> to find a center near you.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions or to apply by phone, call:</p>

<ul>
	<li>1-800-621-FEMA (3362)</li>
	<li>TTY 1-800-462-7585</li>
	<li>711 and VRS 1-800-621-3362</li>
</ul>
