<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><h3>Additional Assistance and Resources</h3><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">International Terrorism Victim Expense Reimbursement Program (ITVERP)</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Justice</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The International Terrorism Victim Expense Reimbursement Program (ITVERP) is a unique federal program. It reimburses certain expenses of victims of terrorism. A victim... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="International Terrorism Victim Expense Reimbursement Program (ITVERP)" data-agency="U.S. Department of Justice">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The International Terrorism Victim Expense Reimbursement Program (ITVERP) is a unique federal program. It reimburses certain expenses of victims of terrorism. A victim must have suffered direct physical or emotional injury or death due to an act of terrorism abroad.</p>

<p>The conditions below must be met to qualify:</p>

<ul>
	<li>The event must have occurred outside the U.S.</li>
	<li>The expenses must be a direct result of the event.</li>
	<li>The event must be designated an act of international terrorism for ITVERP.</li>
</ul>

<p>You may check for your event on the <a name="U.S._Department_of_Justice__||_U.S._Depa"></a><a href="http://www.ovc.gov/itverp/terrorist_events.html" target="_blank">Terrorist Incident Designation List</a>. Once your event is on the list, you may submit the related expenses for victims who qualify. If your event is not on the list, ITVERP staff will submit a request for designation.</p>

<p>Related expenses may include:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Medical (including dental and rehabilitation)</li>
	<li>Mental health care</li>
	<li>Property loss, repair, replacement</li>
	<li>Funeral and burial</li>
	<li>Miscellaneous expenses (like temporary lodging, local transportation, telephone, emergency travel)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>To qualify, at the time of the event you must have been:</p>

<ul>
	<li>A U.S. citizen</li>
	<li>A U.S. employee</li>
	<li>A U.S. government contractor, including foreign nationals</li>
</ul>

<p>A family member or legal designee may apply for a victim who is a minor, incompetent, incapacitated, or killed. You may also apply if, along with the victim, you are a:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Spouse</li>
	<li>Parent</li>
	<li>Child</li>
	<li>Sibling</li>
	<li>Legal designee</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>Go to the <a href="http://www.ovc.gov/itverp/documents.html#forms" target="_blank">Forms and Checklists</a> page on the <a href="http://www.ovc.gov/itverp" target="_blank">ITVERP</a> website for more details and an application.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>Contact ITVERP to learn more:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Call: 1-800-363-0441</li>
	<li>Write to:</li>
</ul>

<p>Office for Victims of Crime<br />
ITVERP Resource Center<br />
810 7th Street, N.W.<br />
Washington, DC 20531</p>

<ul>
	<li>Email: <a name="U.S._Department_of_Justice_||_U.S._Depar"></a><a href="mailto:ITVERP@usdoj.gov">ITVERP@usdoj.gov</a></li>
</ul>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">State Crime Victims Compensation</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Justice</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>State victim assistance and compensation programs are services that can help victims recover after a crime. Victims of Crime Act (VOCA) grants supplement state funds that... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="State Crime Victims Compensation" data-agency="U.S. Department of Justice">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>State victim assistance and compensation programs are services that can help victims recover after a crime. Victims of Crime Act (VOCA) grants supplement state funds that reimburse victims for crime-related expenses. Eligible expenses may include the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Medical costs</li>
	<li>Mental health counseling</li>
	<li>Funeral and burial costs</li>
	<li>Lost wages or loss of support</li>
</ul>

<p>Every state, the District of Columbia, and U.S. territories have programs for crime victims. Each state offers their own programs, but most have similar eligibility requirements and benefits. Maximum awards may vary by state, but could range from $10,000 to $25,000.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>You may only get payment when other sources like insurance or legal awards don't cover the loss. Some expenses, including the following, are not covered by most programs:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Theft</li>
	<li>Damage</li>
	<li>Property loss</li>
</ul>

<p>State programs are also not required to pay in terrorism cases.</p>

<p>You must comply with all state rules to qualify. You must also assist with reasonable police requests and submit a timely application to the program.</p>

<p>You can find links on the <a href="http://www.ojp.usdoj.gov/ovc/" target="_blank">Office for Victims of Crime (OVC)</a> site for different crime victim resources and programs, and their state contacts. Requirements will vary by program.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>You may qualify for benefits, including reimbursement of certain costs, if you are the victim of a crime. Contact your state or territory OVC office for application information.</p>

<p>You may find contacts for each state program on the <a href="http://ojp.gov/ovc/map.html" target="_blank">U.S. Resource Map of Crime Victim Services &amp; Information</a> page.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>To learn more, you may send an email to us on the <a href="http://ovc.ncjrs.gov/askovc/" target="_blank">AskOVC</a> page.</p>

<p>You may also call our OVC Resource Center:</p>

<ul>
	<li>1-800-851-3420</li>
	<li>301-519-5500</li>
	<li>TTY 1-877-712-9279</li>
</ul>

<p>Or write to:</p>

<p style="margin-left: 30px">Office for Victims of Crime<br />
U.S. Department of Justice<br />
810 Seventh Street NW., 8th Floor<br />
Washington, DC 20531</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">Savings Bond Redemption and Replacement</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of the Treasury</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>If you live in a presidentially declared disaster area, you may be able to redeem savings bonds early, before the end of the 12-month holding period. Check the... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Savings Bond Redemption and Replacement" data-agency="U.S. Department of the Treasury">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>If you live in a presidentially declared disaster area, you may be able to redeem savings bonds early, before the end of the 12-month holding period. Check the TreasuryDirect <a href="http://treasurydirect.gov/news/news.htm" target="_blank">Press Room</a> page to see if any financial companies in your area may redeem bonds early.</p>

<p>You may also be able to get faster replacement of any paper bonds lost or destroyed in a disaster.</p>

<p>You may ask to both redeem and replace a savings bond if it meets the conditions below:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Its less than 12 months old, and</li>
	<li>It was lost or destroyed in a disaster.</li>
</ul>

<p>As of January 1, 2012, we no longer sell or issue paper bonds as replacements. <a href="http://treasurydirect.gov/indiv/myaccount/myaccount_treasurydirect.htm" target="_blank">TreasuryDirect</a> now issues only electronic bonds. This supports the U.S. Treasurys goal to increase the use of electronic trade.</p>

<p>Take a <a href="http://www.treasurydirect.gov/indiv/TDTour/default.htm" target="_blank">guided tour</a> to learn more about TreasuryDirect.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>To qualify, you must meet both of the conditions below:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Have a bond thats been lost or destroyed.</li>
	<li>Live in a presidentially declared disaster area.</li>
</ul>

<p>No evidence of hardship or property damage is required.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>Learn how to <a href="http://www.treasurydirect.gov/indiv/research/indepth/ebonds/res_e_bonds_eeredeem_disaster.htm" target="_blank">Redeem or Replace Bonds in Areas Affected by Disasters</a>. You can also learn about <a href="http://www.treasurydirect.gov/indiv/research/indepth/ebonds/res_e_bonds_eereplace.htm" target="_blank">Replacing or Reissuing a Paper EE Bond</a>.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>Contact us by phone with savings bond questions:</p>

<ul>
	<li>1-800-553-2663</li>
</ul>

<p>Or email us:</p>

<ul>
	<li><a href="http://treasurydirect.gov/WF/WebFeedback?site=td01&amp;subject=eeori" target="_blank">Electronic EE and I Savings Bonds (TreasuryDirect)</a></li>
	<li><a href="http://treasurydirect.gov/WF/WebFeedback?site=td01&amp;subject=peori" target="_blank">Paper E, EE, and I Savings Bonds</a></li>
</ul>

<p>To contact us by mail, visit our <a href="http://treasurydirect.gov/write.htm" target="_blank">Write Us</a> page to find an address that best fits your topic of need.</p>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">Substance Abuse and Mental Health Services Administration (SAMHSA) Disaster Relief Information</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Health and Human Services</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>The Substance Abuse and Mental Health Services Administrations (SAMHSA) mission is to reduce the impact of substance abuse and mental illness on Americas communities. It... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="Substance Abuse and Mental Health Services Administration (SAMHSA) Disaster Relief Information" data-agency="U.S. Department of Health and Human Services">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>The Substance Abuse and Mental Health Services Administrations (SAMHSA) mission is to reduce the impact of substance abuse and mental illness on Americas communities. It helps prepare states and communities to provide an effective response after a disaster.<br />
<br />
<b><i>If you or someone you know needs help right now, please use the resources below to find help:</i></b></p>

<ul>
	<li><b><a href="https://www.suicidepreventionlifeline.org/" target="_blank">National Suicide Prevention Lifeline</a> 1-800-273-TALK (8255)</b>  If youre in a suicidal or emotional crisis, please call this 24-hour hotline to reach a crisis center. You may also use the <a href="https://www.suicidepreventionlifeline.org/GetHelp/LifelineChat.aspx" target="_blank">Lifeline Crisis Chat</a> found on the site.</li>
	<li><b><a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/find-help/disaster-distress-helpline" target="_blank">Disaster Distress Helpline</a> 1-800-985-5990</b>  Call to get help with common reactions like stress, anxiety, and depression. The helpline can also guide you to more information, support, and counseling to help you cope.</li>
	<li><b><a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/find-help/national-helpline" target="_blank">SAMHSAs National Helpline</a> 1-800-662-HELP (4357)</b> or <b>TDD 1-800-487-4889</b>  Get help for mental and substance use disorders, prevention, and recovery. This is a free, 24-hour, confidential treatment referral and information service. (English &amp; Spanish)</li>
	<li><b><a href="https://findtreatment.samhsa.gov/" target="_blank">Behavioral Health Treatment Services Locator</a></b>  Find alcohol, drug abuse, and mental health treatment services around the country.</li>
</ul>

<p><b>You can also visit the <a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/treatment/index.aspx" target="_blank">Find Help</a> page for other crisis help and treatment locations.</b><br />
<br />
Below is a list of some of SAMHSAs Disaster Behavioral Health services.<br />
<br />
<b>Crisis Counseling Assistance and Training Program (CCP)</b><br />
<br />
The CCP is a grant program for mental health authorities funded by FEMA and administered by SAMHSA.<br />
<br />
The program can offer you and your community help to aid in recovery from the effects of disasters. It does this through community-based outreach and educational services.<br />
<br />
<b>SAMHSA Disaster Technical Assistance Center (SAMHSA DTAC)</b><br />
<br />
The SAMHSA DTAC helps prepare approved entities to deliver an effective mental health and substance abuse response to disasters. These include the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>States,</li>
	<li>Territories,</li>
	<li>Federally recognized tribes, and</li>
	<li>Other local entities.</li>
</ul>

<p>Services offered include:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Technical assistance, training, and consultation.</li>
	<li>Disaster behavioral health resources.</li>
	<li>Information exchange and knowledge brokering.</li>
</ul>

<p><b>SAMHSA Disaster Distress Helpline (SAMHSA DDH)</b><br />
<br />
The SAMHSA DDH is a national hotline that offers year-round disaster crisis counseling. If you feel distressed after a disaster, and live in the U.S. or its territories, you can use this service. Its toll-free, multilingual, crisis support, and is available 24 hours a day, 7 days a week.</p>

<ul>
	<li>You can call or text to connect to trained counselors at the closest crisis counseling center.</li>
	<li>Helpline staff provides counseling and support, and can help you learn how to cope with common stress reactions. They can also provide referrals to local resources for follow-up care.</li>
	<li>To learn more, visit the <a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/find-help/disaster-distress-helpline" target="_blank">SAMHSA</a> website.</li>
</ul>

<p><b>SAMHSA Disaster App</b><br />
<br />
The Disaster App makes it easy for disaster responders to provide quality support to survivors. From the touch of a button, you can learn about:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Pre-deployment preparation,</li>
	<li>On-the-ground assistance,</li>
	<li>Post-deployment resources, and more.</li>
</ul>

<p>You can share resources, like tips for helping survivors cope, and find local behavioral health services. Responders at all stages of deployment can also find self-care support.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>SAMHSA's website offers free information and resources to anyone who is in crisis, or with or at risk for substance abuse and mental health problems. Theres also information for families, caregivers, and service providers.<br />
<br />
<b><i>If you need help right away, the site offers several crisis lines you can call to <a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/find-help" target="_blank">find help</a>.</i></b><br />
<br />
The CCP requires a presidential disaster declaration before states, territories, and federally recognized tribes may apply.<br />
<br />
SAMHSA DTAC offers free services and materials to support disaster behavioral health professionals and other first responders. Many of the resources are available to everyone on the DTAC site.<br />
<br />
The SAMHSA Disaster App is also free and is available to disaster responders on iPhone, Android, and BlackBerry devices.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>The services below are free and available with no application process:</p>

<ul>
	<li>SAMHSA Disaster Distress Hotline, and</li>
	<li>SAMHSA Disaster App (for disaster responders).</li>
</ul>

<p>For states, territories, tribes, and other local entities, please use the <b>CCP</b> and <b>SAMHSA DTAC</b> contacts below to learn more.</p>

<p>Please contact the<b>Disaster Distress Helpline</b>to talk with someone. Its free, multilingual and available 24 hours a day, 7 days a week.</p>

	<li>Call<strong>1-800-985-5990</strong>or TTY<strong>1-800-846-8517</strong>.</li>
	<li>Text<strong>TalkWithUs</strong>to<strong>66746</strong>.</li>
	<li>You can also visit the<a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/find-help/disaster-distress-helpline" target="_blank">Disaster Distress Helpline</a>page.</li>
</ul>

<ul>
	<li>Call 1-240-276-0408.</li>
	<li>Send email to<a href="mailto:Erik.hierholzer@samhsa.hhs.gov" target="_blank">Erik.hierholzer@samhsa.hhs.gov</a>.</li>
	<li>Visit the<a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/dtac/ccp" target="_blank">CCP</a>page.</li>
</ul>

</ul>

	<li>Visit the<a href="https://store.samhsa.gov/apps/disaster/" target="_blank">SAMHSADisaster App</a>website.</li>
</ul>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row odd "><h4 class="program_title">203(h) Mortgage Insurance for Disaster Victims and 203(k) Rehabilitation Mortgage Insurance</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>Section 203(h) Mortgage Insurance for Disaster Victims helps make it easier for survivors to get a mortgage to buy or rebuild a... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="203(h) Mortgage Insurance for Disaster Victims and 203(k) Rehabilitation Mortgage Insurance" data-agency="U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p><strong>Section 203(h) Mortgage Insurance for Disaster Victims</strong> helps make it easier for survivors to get a mortgage to buy or rebuild a home.</p>

<p><strong>Section 203(k) Rehabilitation Mortgage Insurance</strong> offers two options for both home buyers and homeowners:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Get a single mortgage to buy or refinance a home and the cost of its rehabilitation, or</li>
	<li>Finance the rehabilitation of your existing home.</li>
</ul>

<p>You may use the money for work ranging from minor to a total rebuild. This could include the following:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Residential section rehabilitation of a property that also has non-residential uses.</li>
	<li>Conversion of any size property to a one- to four-unit structure.</li>
</ul>

<p>For smaller repairs or rehabilitation, up to $35,000, you may be able to get a <strong>Limited 203(k)</strong>. This is for work that doesnt require you to buy or refinance the property.</p>

<p>To learn more, visit the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) program pages below:</p>

<ul>
	<li><a href="http://portal.hud.gov/hudportal/HUD?src=/program_offices/housing/sfh/ins/203h-dft" target="_blank">Mortgage Insurance for Disaster Victims Section 203(h)</a>, or</li>
	<li><a href="http://portal.hud.gov/hudportal/HUD?src=/program_offices/housing/sfh/203k/203k--df" target="_blank">Section 203(k) Rehabilitation Mortgage Insurance</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>You must meet the conditions below to qualify for these programs.</p>

<p>Section 203(h) Mortgage Insurance for Disaster Victims:</p>

<ul>
	<li>You must own a one-family home damaged or destroyed in a presidentially declared disaster, and</li>
	<li>You must live in the home.</li>
</ul>

<p>Section 203(k) Rehabilitation Mortgage Insurance:</p>

<ul>
	<li>You must be able to make monthly mortgage payments, and</li>
	<li>You must be rehabilitating a home thats at least one year old.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>To apply, view the <a name="U.S._Department_of_Housing_and_Urban_Dev"></a><a href="https://portal.hud.gov/hudportal/HUD?src=/program_offices/housing/sfh/lender/lenderlist" target="_blank">lender list</a> to find an approved lender near you.</p>

<p>If you apply under Section 203(h), you must send your application to the lender within one year of the disaster declaration.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions, contact our <a href="http://portal.hud.gov/hudportal/HUD?src=/program_offices/housing/sfh/fharesourcectr" target="_blank">FHA Resource Center</a>. Or you may call us at the phone numbers below:</p>

<ul>
	<li>1-800-CALL-FHA (1-800-225-5342)</li>
	<li>TTY 1-800-877-8339</li>
</ul>

<p>You may also use one of these other contacts to learn more:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Visit the <a href="http://portal.hud.gov/hudportal/HUD?src=/program_offices/housing/sfh/sfhhocs" target="_blank">FHA Homeownership Center</a> page to locate a center near you.</li>
	<li>Email us at <a href="mailto:answers@hud.gov">answers@hud.gov</a>.</li>
	<li>Contact a <a href="http://portal.hud.gov/hudportal/HUD?src=/i_want_to/talk_to_a_housing_counselor" target="_blank">HUD-approved housing counseling agency</a> at 1-800-569-4287.</li>
</ul>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div><div class="row even "><h4 class="program_title">FEMA Disaster Recovery Center (DRC) / DRC Locator</h4><p class="agency"><strong>Managing Agency: </strong>U.S. Department of Homeland Security/FEMA</p><div class="program_description_intro"><strong>Program Description: </strong>FEMA Disaster Recovery Centers (DRCs) are accessible facilities and mobile offices set up after a disaster. Theyre set up in convenient locations to make them easier to... <a class="read_more questionnaire-foa-read-more" href="javascript:void(0);" data-foa="FEMA Disaster Recovery Center (DRC) / DRC Locator" data-agency="U.S. Department of Homeland Security/FEMA">Read More</a></div><div class="program_description" style="display: none"><strong>Program Description: </strong><p>FEMA Disaster Recovery Centers (DRCs) are accessible facilities and mobile offices set up after a disaster. Theyre set up in convenient locations to make them easier to find. You can visit a DRC to learn more about FEMA and ask questions about your case.</p>

<p>A DRC may also be able to help you:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Apply for assistance.</li>
	<li>Learn more about disaster assistance programs.</li>
	<li>Learn the status of your FEMA application.</li>
	<li>Understand any letters you get from FEMA.</li>
	<li>Find housing and rental assistance information.</li>
	<li>Get referrals to agencies that may offer other assistance.</li>
	<li>Learn about Small Business Administration (SBA) programs.</li>
</ul>

<p>The <strong>DRC Locator</strong> can help you find the locations, hours, and services of DRCs near you.</p>
<p><strong>General Program Requirements</strong></p><p>Anyone can visit a DRC or use the DRC Locator tool.</p>
<p><strong>Application Process</strong></p><p>No application is required.</p>

<p>To find the closest DRC, use the <a href="https://egateway.fema.gov/ESF6/DRCLocator" target="_blank">DRC Locator</a>.</p>

<p>Or text <strong>DRC</strong> and a <b>Zip Code</b> to <b>4FEMA (43362)</b>. Example: <em>DRC 01234</em>.</p>
<p><strong>Program Contact Information</strong></p><p>If you have questions or want to learn more, call:</p>

<ul>
	<li>1-800-621-FEMA (3362)</li>
	<li>TTY 1-800-462-7585</li>
	<li>711 and VRS 1-800-621-3362</li>
</ul>
<a class="read_less" href="javascript:void(0);">Read Less</a></div></div></span>

        <div class="row">
            <div id="applyIntro" class="col-md-12">
                <p>Disclaimer: Completing the questionnaire helps you narrow your search for possible assistance. It does not determine eligibility or guarantee assistance.</p>

            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="row">
            <div class="panel-group col-xs-12" id="accordion">
                <div class="panel panel-default">
                    <div class="panel-heading">
                        <h4 class="panel-title">
                            <a data-toggle="collapse" data-parent="#accordion" href="#collapseOne">What You Need to Apply</a>
                        </h4>
                    </div>
                    <div id="collapseOne" class="panel-collapse collapse">
                        <div class="panel-body"><p>Before you start your application, please have the information below and a pen and paper ready.</p>

<h3><strong>Social Security Number</strong></h3>

<p><em><strong>You, another adult member or minor child in your household must have a Social Security number. You or they must also be a U.S. citizen, non-citizen national, or qualified alien.</strong></em></p>

<p>If you don't have a Social Security number, read the article <em><a href="https://faq.ssa.gov/link/portal/34011/34019/Article/3755/How-do-I-apply-for-a-new-or-replacement-Social-Security-number-card" target="_blank">How do I apply for a new or replacement Social Security number card</a></em>. You will get instructions on what to do and what documents you will need.</p>

<p>Once you have your number, you may come back to <strong>DisasterAssistance.gov</strong> or call FEMA at one of the phone numbers above to apply.</p>

<h3><strong>Insurance Information</strong></h3>

<p>Describe the type(s) of insurance coverage you have. This could include coverage under policies like homeowners, flood, automobile, or mobile home insurance.</p>

<h3><strong>Damage Information</strong></h3>

<p>Describe the damage caused by the disaster. Include the type of disaster (like flood, hurricane, or earthquake) and the type of dwelling or vehicle (like a condo, mobile home or house, or a car or truck).</p>

<h3><strong>Financial Information</strong></h3>

<p>Provide your total annual household income, before taxes, at the time of the disaster.</p>

<h3><strong>Contact Information</strong></h3>

<p>Provide the address and phone number of the property where the damage occurred and the address and phone number of where we can reach you now.</p>

<h3><strong>Direct Deposit Information <em>(optional)</em></strong></h3>

<p>If approved, we can deposit your funds directly into your bank account. You just need to provide the following banking information:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Bank name</li>
	<li>Type of account (like checking or savings)</li>
	<li>Routing number</li>
	<li>Account number</li>
</ul>

<p><strong><em>NEED HELP? </em></strong>If you need help with the application, please call FEMA at one of the phone numbers above.</p>
</div>
                    </div>
                </div>
                <div class="text">
                    <p>Based on your answers to this questionnaire, you may be eligible for the following forms of assistance. Review the forms of assistance carefully. Review what you need to apply and have the materials ready before you begin.<br />
<br />
Some forms of assistance allow you to apply directly online using DisasterAssistance.gov. Other forms of assistance require you to follow additional instructions, such as visiting another agencys website, to apply.</p>

                </div>
